	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Martin Garrix</h1>
	<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
		<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
		<div id="contentSub"></div>
		<div id="contentSub2"></div>

<div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Dutch DJ and record producer</div>

<p><b>Martijn Gerard Garritsen</b> (<small>Dutch:&#160;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Dutch" title="Help:IPA/Dutch">[mɑrˈtɛi̯n ɣəˈrɑrt ˈxɑrɪtsə(n)]</a></span>; born 14 May 1996),<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> professionally known as <b>Martin Garrix</b> and under other pseudonyms such as Ytram<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> and GRX,<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> is a Dutch DJ and record producer. His most known singles are "<a href="/wiki/Animals_(Martin_Garrix_song)" title="Animals (Martin Garrix song)">Animals</a>", "<a href="/wiki/In_the_Name_of_Love_(Martin_Garrix_and_Bebe_Rexha_song)" title="In the Name of Love (Martin Garrix and Bebe Rexha song)">In the Name of Love</a>", and "<a href="/wiki/Scared_to_Be_Lonely" title="Scared to Be Lonely">Scared to Be Lonely</a>". He was ranked number one on <i><a href="/wiki/DJ_Mag" title="DJ Mag">DJ Mag</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s Top 100 DJs list for three consecutive years (2016, 2017, and 2018).
</p><p>He has performed at music festivals such as <a href="/wiki/Coachella_Valley_Music_and_Arts_Festival" title="Coachella Valley Music and Arts Festival">Coachella</a>, <a href="/wiki/Electric_Daisy_Carnival" title="Electric Daisy Carnival">Electric Daisy Carnival</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ultra_Music_Festival" title="Ultra Music Festival">Ultra Music Festival</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tomorrowland_(festival)" title="Tomorrowland (festival)">Tomorrowland</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Creamfields" title="Creamfields">Creamfields</a>. In 2014 he headlined the 1st edition of <a href="/wiki/Ultra_South_Africa" title="Ultra South Africa">Ultra South Africa</a> making this his first major festival. In the same year he became the youngest DJ to headline 2014 Ultra Music Festival at the age of 17. He was a resident DJ at Spain's Hï Ibiza (2017) and <a href="/wiki/Ushua%C3%AFa_Ibiza_Beach_Hotel" title="Ushuaïa Ibiza Beach Hotel">Ushuaïa Ibiza</a> (2016 and 2018). He founded the label <a href="/wiki/Stmpd_Rcrds" title="Stmpd Rcrds">Stmpd Rcrds</a> in 2016, months after leaving <a href="/wiki/Spinnin%27_Records" title="Spinnin&#39; Records">Spinnin' Records</a> and before signing with <a href="/wiki/Sony_Music" title="Sony Music">Sony Music</a>.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span></h2>
<p>Garrix was born as Martijn Gerard Garritsen on 14 May 1996 in <a href="/wiki/Amstelveen" title="Amstelveen">Amstelveen</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a>, the son of Gerard and Karin Garritsen. He has a younger sister named Laura.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Forbes1_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Forbes1-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> He showed musical interest at an early age and learned to play the guitar at the age of 8.
</p><p>In 2004, he expressed interest in becoming a DJ after seeing Dutch DJ <a href="/wiki/Ti%C3%ABsto" title="Tiësto">Tiësto</a> perform at that year's <a href="/wiki/2004_Summer_Olympics_opening_ceremony" title="2004 Summer Olympics opening ceremony">Summer Olympics Opening Ceremony</a> in Athens. He took particular inspiration from the track "<a href="/wiki/Traffic_(Ti%C3%ABsto_song)" title="Traffic (Tiësto song)">Traffic</a>", prompting him to download the specialist <a href="/wiki/Digital_audio_workstation" title="Digital audio workstation">digital audio workstation</a> <a href="/wiki/FL_Studio" title="FL Studio">FL Studio</a>, enabling him to start producing.
</p><p>In 2013, he graduated from the <a href="/wiki/Herman_Brood_Academy" class="mw-redirect" title="Herman Brood Academy">Herman Brood Academy</a>, a production school in <a href="/wiki/Utrecht" title="Utrecht">Utrecht</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Career">Career</span></h2>
<h3><span id="2012.E2.80.932014:_Spinnin.27_Records_deal.2C_.22Animals.22.2C_and_Gold_Skies"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2012–2014:_Spinnin'_Records_deal,_&quot;Animals&quot;,_and_Gold_Skies">2012–2014: Spinnin' Records deal, "Animals", and <i>Gold Skies</i></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Martin_Garrix_Logo_2012.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Martin_Garrix_Logo_2012.png/220px-Martin_Garrix_Logo_2012.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="85" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Martin_Garrix_Logo_2012.png/330px-Martin_Garrix_Logo_2012.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Martin_Garrix_Logo_2012.png/440px-Martin_Garrix_Logo_2012.png 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="310" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Martin_Garrix_Logo_2012.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Martin Garrix's logo, 2012–2015</div></div></div>
<p>Garrix was discovered by Tiësto, whom he described as inspirational, humble, and legendary.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> He had his beginnings with the songs "BFAM", a collaboration with Dutch DJ <a href="/wiki/Julian_Jordan_(DJ)" class="mw-redirect" title="Julian Jordan (DJ)">Julian Jordan</a>, and "Just Some Loops", a collaboration with TV Noise. In the documentary <a href="/wiki/What_We_Started" title="What We Started">What We Started</a>, Garrix describes how he was discovered by the Dutch record label <a href="/wiki/Spinnin%27_Records" title="Spinnin&#39; Records">Spinnin' Records</a> following the release of his remix for the <a href="/wiki/Enrique_Iglesias" title="Enrique Iglesias">Enrique Iglesias</a> single "Tonight (I'm Loving You)". He signed with Spinnin' Records in 2012, releasing "Error 404", a collaboration with Dutch DJ <a href="/wiki/Jay_Hardway" title="Jay Hardway">Jay Hardway</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Beatport1_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Beatport1-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> In 2013, Garrix co-released "Torrent" with Dutch DJ <a href="/wiki/Sidney_Samson" title="Sidney Samson">Sidney Samson</a> on Tiësto's Musical Freedom label.<sup id="cite_ref-Billboard1_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard1-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Martin_Garrix_2013.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Martin_Garrix_2013.jpg/220px-Martin_Garrix_2013.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Martin_Garrix_2013.jpg/330px-Martin_Garrix_2013.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Martin_Garrix_2013.jpg/440px-Martin_Garrix_2013.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1250" data-file-height="833" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Martin_Garrix_2013.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Martin Garrix at Midsummer White Festival 2013</div></div></div><p> Garrix gained fame through his solo release, "<a href="/wiki/Animals_(Martin_Garrix_song)" title="Animals (Martin Garrix song)">Animals</a>",<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> which was released on 16 June 2013. The single became a hit in several countries in Europe, and allowed Garrix to become the youngest person to reach number one on <a href="/wiki/Beatport" title="Beatport">Beatport</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> The track appears on Dutch DJ <a href="/wiki/Hardwell" title="Hardwell">Hardwell</a>'s album, <i><a href="/wiki/Hardwell_presents_%27Revealed_Volume_4%27" class="mw-redirect" title="Hardwell presents &#39;Revealed Volume 4&#39;">Hardwell presents 'Revealed Volume 4'</a></i>. On 30 September, Garrix released a remix of "Project T" by Sander Van Doorn and Belgian-Greek DJ duo <a href="/wiki/Dimitri_Vegas_%26_Like_Mike" title="Dimitri Vegas &amp; Like Mike">Dimitri Vegas &amp; Like Mike</a> which quickly hit number one on the Beatport charts.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> He appeared on <i>DJ Magazine</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s top 100 DJs list in 2013 as a new entry at number 40.
</p><p>In November 2013, Garrix signed a deal with American entertainment company <a href="/wiki/Scooter_Braun#SB_Projects" title="Scooter Braun">Scooter Braun Projects</a>, making Garrix the company's first EDM client. The deal was split-worldwide management with MusicAllStars Management, sister company of Spinnin’ Records, since Garrix was already signed to Spinnin’ Records.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In December 2013, he released "<a href="/wiki/Wizard_(Martin_Garrix_song)" class="mw-redirect" title="Wizard (Martin Garrix song)">Wizard</a>" with Jay Hardway which peaked at number 6 in Belgium and number 17 in the Netherlands. In 2014, Garrix collaborated with Dutch duo <a href="/wiki/Firebeatz" title="Firebeatz">Firebeatz</a> on "Helicopter" which reached number one on the Beatport Top 100 charts for two weeks. He also produced the <a href="/wiki/Sensation_(event)" title="Sensation (event)">Sensation 2014</a> anthem, "<a href="/wiki/Tremor_(song)" title="Tremor (song)">Tremor</a>", along with Dimitri Vegas &amp; Like Mike.
</p><p>Garrix performed at <a href="/wiki/Ultra_Music_Festival" title="Ultra Music Festival">Ultra Music Festival</a> 2014, where he debuted several new and unreleased tracks, including collaborations with American DJ <a href="/wiki/Dillon_Francis" title="Dillon Francis">Dillon Francis</a>, Hardwell, and Dutch DJ <a href="/wiki/Afrojack" title="Afrojack">Afrojack</a>. In June, he collaborated with Dutch DJ <a href="/wiki/Sander_van_Doorn" title="Sander van Doorn">Sander van Doorn</a> and Canadian duo <a href="/wiki/DVBBS" class="mw-redirect" title="DVBBS">DVBBS</a> on "<a href="/wiki/Gold_Skies" title="Gold Skies">Gold Skies</a>". This was his first vocal track which featured the singer Aleesia.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> He also released the track "<a href="/wiki/Proxy_(song)" title="Proxy (song)">Proxy</a>" for free download. Most of these songs were featured on Garrix's debut EP, <i><a href="/wiki/Gold_Skies_(EP)" title="Gold Skies (EP)">Gold Skies</a></i>, which was released on 8 July 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>After the release of his debut EP, Garrix continued to collaborate with mainstream DJs. The first of such collaborations being a song with Dutch DJ <a href="/wiki/MOTi" class="mw-redirect" title="MOTi">MOTi</a> called "<a href="/wiki/Virus_(How_About_Now)" title="Virus (How About Now)">Virus (How About Now)</a>", followed by a collaboration with Afrojack called "<a href="/wiki/Turn_Up_the_Speakers" title="Turn Up the Speakers">Turn Up the Speakers</a>" which Afrojack and Garrix both premiered at Ultra Music Festival.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> In 2014, he appeared on <i>DJ Magazine</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s top 100 DJs list at number 4.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="2015:_Collaborations_and_Spinnin.27_contract_termination"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2015:_Collaborations_and_Spinnin'_contract_termination">2015: Collaborations and Spinnin' contract termination</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Martin_Garrix_Logo_2015.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Martin_Garrix_Logo_2015.png/220px-Martin_Garrix_Logo_2015.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="148" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Martin_Garrix_Logo_2015.png/330px-Martin_Garrix_Logo_2015.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Martin_Garrix_Logo_2015.png/440px-Martin_Garrix_Logo_2015.png 2x" data-file-width="1003" data-file-height="673" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Martin_Garrix_Logo_2015.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Garrix's "+×" logo since 2015</div></div></div><p>In 2015, Garrix experimented with progressive house and started producing progressive tracks aside from his signature big room sound. On 6 February, he released the track "<a href="/wiki/Forbidden_Voices_(song)" title="Forbidden Voices (song)">Forbidden Voices</a>" as a gift to his fans after his Facebook page reached 10 million likes.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In February 2015, he released the single "<a href="/wiki/Don%27t_Look_Down_(Martin_Garrix_song)" title="Don&#39;t Look Down (Martin Garrix song)">Don't Look Down</a>" featuring Grammy-winner <a href="/wiki/Usher_(singer)" class="mw-redirect" title="Usher (singer)">Usher</a>. He also released two video versions for it on <a href="/wiki/Vevo" title="Vevo">Vevo</a>, "Towel Boy" and "Towel Girl". The track was written by Garrix, <a href="/wiki/James_%27JHart%27_Abrahart" class="mw-redirect" title="James &#39;JHart&#39; Abrahart">James 'JHart' Abrahart</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Busbee" title="Busbee">Busbee</a>. It peaked at number three on the <i>Billboard</i> <a href="/wiki/Dance_Club_Songs" title="Dance Club Songs">Dance Club Songs</a>. In an interview with British media company <i><a href="/wiki/DigitalSpy" class="mw-redirect" title="DigitalSpy">DigitalSpy</a></i> in early 2015, Garrix noted that Usher is a "humble" artist and a great collaborator to whom he can directly give input.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Garrix also worked with multi-Grammy winner <a href="/wiki/Ed_Sheeran" title="Ed Sheeran">Ed Sheeran</a> on a track called "<b>Rewind Repeat It</b>" which he played at Ultra Music Festival in Miami in March 2015. On 4 May, he released a track with Tiësto, called "<a href="/wiki/The_Only_Way_Is_Up_(Martin_Garrix_and_Ti%C3%ABsto_song)" title="The Only Way Is Up (Martin Garrix and Tiësto song)">The Only Way Is Up</a>". On 22 May, Swedish DJ <a href="/wiki/Avicii" title="Avicii">Avicii</a> released a lyric video of the song "<a href="/wiki/Waiting_for_Love_(Avicii_song)" title="Waiting for Love (Avicii song)">Waiting for Love</a>" which was co-produced by Garrix. On 6 July, Garrix released the <i><a href="/wiki/Break_Through_the_Silence_(EP)" class="mw-redirect" title="Break Through the Silence (EP)">Break Through the Silence</a></i> dual single with Russian DJs <a href="/wiki/Matisse_and_Sadko" class="mw-redirect" title="Matisse and Sadko">Matisse and Sadko</a>, consisting of the songs "<a href="/wiki/Break_Through_the_Silence_(song)" class="mw-redirect" title="Break Through the Silence (song)">Break Through the Silence</a>" and "Dragon". On 31 October, he released a track titled "<a href="/wiki/Poison_(Martin_Garrix_song)" class="mw-redirect" title="Poison (Martin Garrix song)">Poison</a>" as a promotional single. On 31 December, Garrix released "<a href="/wiki/Bouncybob_(song)" class="mw-redirect" title="Bouncybob (song)">Bouncybob</a>", his final track of the year, for free which he had co-produced with Justin Mylo and <a href="/wiki/Mesto_(DJ)" class="mw-redirect" title="Mesto (DJ)">Mesto</a>.
</p><p>On 26 August 2015, Garrix announced that he had left <a href="/wiki/Spinnin%27_Records" title="Spinnin&#39; Records">Spinnin' Records</a> and MusicAllStars Management due to a conflict over the ownership of his music.<sup id="cite_ref-Billboard2_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard2-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> A point of contention was the release of "Animals" which appeared when Garrix was 17 years old.<sup id="cite_ref-Billboard3_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard3-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> He also announced that he had filed a lawsuit against his then-manager Eelko van Kooten.<sup id="cite_ref-Billboard3_31-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard3-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> In November 2015, Garrix announced that he would be creating his own record label.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> He also went on to sue his manager, Eelko van Kooten, stating that he was told "false and misleading information" before signing with <a href="/wiki/Spinnin%27_Records" title="Spinnin&#39; Records">Spinnin' Records</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 2 December 2015, Garrix reportedly settled with Spinnin' Records in their ongoing legal dispute over the ownership rights of his music. He released a statement confirming that he had withdrawn the summary proceedings after his former record label transferred the ownership rights of his music to him, granted that exclusive licence of all his tracks released before August 2015 will be retained by Spinnin' Records for an undisclosed period.<sup id="cite_ref-Billboard2_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard2-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> However, Garrix also stated that their other outstanding disagreements will likely be the subject of further legal proceedings.<sup id="cite_ref-Billboard2_30-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard2-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="2016:_Launch_of_Stmpd_Rcrds.2C_Sony_record_deal.2C_documentary_and_awards"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2016:_Launch_of_Stmpd_Rcrds,_Sony_record_deal,_documentary_and_awards">2016: Launch of Stmpd Rcrds, Sony record deal, documentary and awards</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Martin_Garrix_@_VELD_Festival.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Martin_Garrix_%40_VELD_Festival.jpg/220px-Martin_Garrix_%40_VELD_Festival.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Martin_Garrix_%40_VELD_Festival.jpg/330px-Martin_Garrix_%40_VELD_Festival.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Martin_Garrix_%40_VELD_Festival.jpg/440px-Martin_Garrix_%40_VELD_Festival.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5859" data-file-height="3911" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Martin_Garrix_@_VELD_Festival.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Martin Garrix live at <a href="/wiki/VELD_Music_Festival" title="VELD Music Festival">VELD Music Festival</a>, 2016</div></div></div>
<p>Garrix launched his own record label called <a href="/wiki/Stmpd_Rcrds" title="Stmpd Rcrds">Stmpd Rcrds</a> in the first quarter of 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> Speaking about the label, he said that he wanted it to be a 'platform' for artists of various genres.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> On 11 March 2016, he released his first single via Stmpd Rcrds titled "<a href="/wiki/Now_That_I%27ve_Found_You" title="Now That I&#39;ve Found You">Now That I've Found You</a>", featuring the vocals of <a href="/wiki/John_Martin_(singer)" title="John Martin (singer)">John Martin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Michel_Zitron" title="Michel Zitron">Michel Zitron</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>
On 18 March 2016, he made use of his one-hour set to premiere ten new unreleased tracks at Ultra Music Festival, including collaborations with <a href="/wiki/Jay_Hardway" title="Jay Hardway">Jay Hardway</a>, <a href="/wiki/Julian_Jordan_(DJ)" class="mw-redirect" title="Julian Jordan (DJ)">Julian Jordan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ed_Sheeran" title="Ed Sheeran">Ed Sheeran</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bebe_Rexha" title="Bebe Rexha">Bebe Rexha</a>, <a href="/wiki/Third_Party_(DJs)" title="Third Party (DJs)">Third Party</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Linkin_Park" title="Linkin Park">Linkin Park</a><sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> along with <a href="/wiki/Area21" title="Area21">Area21</a>, Garrix's duo with <a href="/wiki/Maejor" title="Maejor">Maejor</a>. On 27 May 2016, he released his second single "<a href="/wiki/Lions_in_the_Wild_(Martin_Garrix_song)" class="mw-redirect" title="Lions in the Wild (Martin Garrix song)">Lions in the Wild</a>" with British DJ duo Third Party. On 13 June 2016, Garrix released a promotional single titled "Oops" which became the <a href="/wiki/Electronic_Entertainment_Expo_2016" class="mw-redirect" title="Electronic Entertainment Expo 2016">Electronic Entertainment Expo 2016</a> anthem.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> </p><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Martin_Garrix_Come_Up_Show_cropped.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Martin_Garrix_Come_Up_Show_cropped.jpg/220px-Martin_Garrix_Come_Up_Show_cropped.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="214" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Martin_Garrix_Come_Up_Show_cropped.jpg/330px-Martin_Garrix_Come_Up_Show_cropped.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Martin_Garrix_Come_Up_Show_cropped.jpg/440px-Martin_Garrix_Come_Up_Show_cropped.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2416" data-file-height="2346" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Martin_Garrix_Come_Up_Show_cropped.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Martin Garrix at VELD 2016</div></div></div>
<p>On 26 July 2016, it was announced that Garrix signed a worldwide contract with <a href="/wiki/Sony_Music_Entertainment" class="mw-redirect" title="Sony Music Entertainment">Sony Music International</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Billboard5_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard5-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> He explained that, "their forward thinking approach to streaming and incredible roster of talented artists combined with their passion and understanding for my vision of the future of my music made this a no brainer."<sup id="cite_ref-Billboard5_39-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard5-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 29 July 2016, he released the track "<a href="/wiki/In_the_Name_of_Love_(Martin_Garrix_and_Bebe_Rexha_song)" title="In the Name of Love (Martin Garrix and Bebe Rexha song)">In the Name of Love</a>" with American singer Bebe Rexha.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> On 22 August 2016, Garrix made his first-ever live performance of his own music, with Rexha on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Tonight_Show_Starring_Jimmy_Fallon" title="The Tonight Show Starring Jimmy Fallon">The Tonight Show Starring Jimmy Fallon</a></i>, accompanied by <i>The Tonight Show</i> house band, The Roots.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 14 October 2016, Garrix announced on social media that he was releasing seven songs for seven days. Several of the released songs have been premiered during his performances at Ultra Music Festival and <a href="/wiki/Tomorrowland_(festival)" title="Tomorrowland (festival)">Tomorrowland Belgium</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> The songs were uploaded onto his <a href="/wiki/YouTube" title="YouTube">YouTube</a> channel as music videos with seven visual artists who live-painted their interpretations of each song.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 19 October 2016, Garrix was named the world's top DJ<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> in <i>DJ Mag's</i> annual Top 100 DJs poll.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-MTV_UK_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MTV_UK-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> Speaking to the press, he said "It feels unreal to have won. I 100 percent did not expect it at all. I've had an amazing year, with awesome shows and amazing fans – I'm so thankful for their support. I didn't even do a campaign, and it just shows how dope the fanbase is."<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>It was announced that Garrix will co-star, alongside British DJ <a href="/wiki/Carl_Cox" title="Carl Cox">Carl Cox</a> in an <a href="/wiki/Electronic_dance_music" title="Electronic dance music">EDM</a>-themed documentary titled "<a href="/wiki/What_We_Started" title="What We Started">What We Started</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-Billboard6_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard6-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> The documentary was directed by Bert Marcus<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> alongside executive producer and music supervisor Pete Tong.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> The documentary was premiered on 15 June 2017 at the LA Film Festival.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 6 November 2016, Garrix won "Best Electronic Act" and "Best World Stage Performance" awards at the <a href="/wiki/MTV_Europe_Music_Awards" title="MTV Europe Music Awards">MTV European Music Awards 2016</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> He was presented his award by American rapper <a href="/wiki/G-Eazy" title="G-Eazy">G-Eazy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-WeGotThisCovered1_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WeGotThisCovered1-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> During the awards ceremony, Garrix performed "In the Name of Love" on stage with Bebe Rexha.<sup id="cite_ref-WeGotThisCovered1_54-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WeGotThisCovered1-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 31 December 2016, Martin Garrix played "Scared to Be Lonely", featuring British singer <a href="/wiki/Dua_Lipa" title="Dua Lipa">Dua Lipa</a>, for the first time while headlining the stage at his first ever show in Myanmar. He released the song on 27 January 2017.
</p>
<h3><span id="2017:_Residency.2C_modeling.2C_legal_victory_and_collaborations"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2017:_Residency,_modeling,_legal_victory_and_collaborations">2017: Residency, modeling, legal victory and collaborations</span></h3>
<p>Garrix announced that he would be supporting Canadian singer <a href="/wiki/Justin_Bieber" title="Justin Bieber">Justin Bieber</a> on his <a href="/wiki/Purpose_World_Tour" title="Purpose World Tour">Purpose World Tour</a> in Australia which began in March and at the '<a href="/wiki/Barclaycard" title="Barclaycard">Barclaycard presents British Summer Time Hyde Park</a>' show on 2 July 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-NME1_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NME1-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 27 January 2017, he released "<a href="/wiki/Scared_to_Be_Lonely" title="Scared to Be Lonely">Scared to Be Lonely</a>" a collaboration with British singer <a href="/wiki/Dua_Lipa" title="Dua Lipa">Dua Lipa</a> as a single. He performed the song with Lipa on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Tonight_Show_Starring_Jimmy_Fallon" title="The Tonight Show Starring Jimmy Fallon">The Tonight Show Starring Jimmy Fallon</a></i> in March<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> before releasing two volumes of extended plays featuring twelve remixes.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Garrix was announced as a resident DJ for the 2017 season at <a href="/wiki/H%C3%AF_Ibiza" class="mw-redirect" title="Hï Ibiza">Hï Ibiza</a>, previously known as <a href="/wiki/Space_(Ibiza_nightclub)" title="Space (Ibiza nightclub)">Space Ibiza</a>, a popular dance-music club owned by Ushuaïa Entertainment. He previously had a DJ residency at Hï Ibiza's sister venue, <a href="/wiki/Ushua%C3%AFa_Ibiza_Beach_Hotel" title="Ushuaïa Ibiza Beach Hotel">Ushuaïa</a> in 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 7 April 2017, "<a href="/wiki/Byte_(song)" title="Byte (song)">Byte</a>", a collaboration with <a href="/wiki/Brooks_(DJ)" title="Brooks (DJ)">Brooks</a>, was released as a single.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> The song was previously debuted by Garrix during his 2017 <a href="/wiki/Ultra_Music_Festival" title="Ultra Music Festival">Ultra Music Festival</a> set in Miami.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>
On 14 April 2017, Garrix debuted a collaboration with Australian singer <a href="/wiki/Troye_Sivan" title="Troye Sivan">Troye Sivan</a>, who later joined him on stage for their performance at the <a href="/wiki/Coachella_Valley_Music_and_Arts_Festival" title="Coachella Valley Music and Arts Festival">Coachella Valley Music And Arts Festival</a> in California.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> The song title was "<a href="/wiki/There_for_You_(Martin_Garrix_and_Troye_Sivan_song)" title="There for You (Martin Garrix and Troye Sivan song)">There for You</a>", as announced by Sivan on Twitter.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> The song was officially released on 26 May 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> </p><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Martin_Garrix_@_World_Club_Dome_Winter_Edition_2017_(2).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Martin_Garrix_%40_World_Club_Dome_Winter_Edition_2017_%282%29.jpg/220px-Martin_Garrix_%40_World_Club_Dome_Winter_Edition_2017_%282%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Martin_Garrix_%40_World_Club_Dome_Winter_Edition_2017_%282%29.jpg/330px-Martin_Garrix_%40_World_Club_Dome_Winter_Edition_2017_%282%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Martin_Garrix_%40_World_Club_Dome_Winter_Edition_2017_%282%29.jpg/440px-Martin_Garrix_%40_World_Club_Dome_Winter_Edition_2017_%282%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4671" data-file-height="3503" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Martin_Garrix_@_World_Club_Dome_Winter_Edition_2017_(2).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Martin Garrix at World Club Dome Winter Edition 2017</div></div></div><p>Garrix appeared as the face of <a href="/wiki/Armani_Exchange" class="mw-redirect" title="Armani Exchange">Armani Exchange</a> in their Fall 2017 campaign, becoming one of the first few internationally recognized DJs to enter modeling.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> Armani Exchange announced it on social media, stating "the face of the new Armani Exchange Fall Winter 2017/2018 campaign: Martin Garrix"<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>At the <a href="/wiki/Tomorrowland" title="Tomorrowland">Tomorrowland</a> 2017 festival, Garrix debuted his YTRAM alias, which spells "Marty" backwards.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> He also premiered the song "<a href="/wiki/So_Far_Away_(Martin_Garrix_and_David_Guetta_song)" title="So Far Away (Martin Garrix and David Guetta song)">So Far Away</a>", a collaboration with French DJ <a href="/wiki/David_Guetta" title="David Guetta">David Guetta</a>, who joined him on stage to perform it,<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> as well as his first solo track in over a year, "<a href="/wiki/Pizza_(song)" title="Pizza (song)">Pizza</a>", which received an official release on 25 August 2017.
</p><p>Garrix was listed in <i><a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a>'</i> World's Highest-Paid DJs 2017 ranking with earnings of $19.5 million for 12 months prior to June 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Details of Garrix's collaborative unreleased song with Ed Sheeran, titled "Replay Rewind" or alternately, "Rewind Repeat It", was published on <a href="/wiki/ASCAP" class="mw-redirect" title="ASCAP">ASCAP</a><sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> with Sony and <a href="/wiki/BDi_Music" class="mw-redirect" title="BDi Music">BDI</a> listed as the publishers of the song. The track was not officially released.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> The song was premiered at the 2015 <a href="/wiki/Ultra_Music_Festival" title="Ultra Music Festival">Ultra Music Festival</a> in Miami<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> and is regularly played by Garrix at music festivals.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 20 September 2017, a Dutch judge ruled in favor of Garrix who regained the rights to his music that were previously signed to Spinnin' Records and MusicAllStars, to have his contract permanently terminated.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> Garrix, who demanded €3.7 million from Spinnin' and €650,000 from MusicAllStars, said "All of (their) claims have been rejected by the court. The only remaining question is the amount to be repaid (to Garrix)."<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In October 2017, Garrix, under the alias GRX, collaborated again with Brooks to release the song "Boomerang".<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> In December 2017, he released "<a href="/wiki/So_Far_Away_(Martin_Garrix_and_David_Guetta_song)" title="So Far Away (Martin Garrix and David Guetta song)">So Far Away</a>" with David Guetta, featuring Romy Dya and Jamie Scott. British singer Ellie Goulding was originally supposed to be featured on the song but her label prevented the release after it was previewed by Garrix at his Tomorrowland set.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="2018:_Closing_the_Winter_Olympics.2C_further_collaborations_and_Bylaw"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2018:_Closing_the_Winter_Olympics,_further_collaborations_and_Bylaw">2018: Closing the Winter Olympics, further collaborations and <i>Bylaw</i></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Garrix_Palmesus_2018.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Garrix_Palmesus_2018.jpg/220px-Garrix_Palmesus_2018.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Garrix_Palmesus_2018.jpg/330px-Garrix_Palmesus_2018.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Garrix_Palmesus_2018.jpg/440px-Garrix_Palmesus_2018.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1067" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Garrix_Palmesus_2018.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Martin Garrix at Palmesus 2018, the stage lighting showing his signature "+×" logo.</div></div></div>
<p>On 23 February 2018, Garrix released his second collaboration with <a href="/wiki/David_Guetta" title="David Guetta">David Guetta</a> and his third with <a href="/wiki/Brooks_(DJ)" title="Brooks (DJ)">Brooks</a> with the song "<a href="/wiki/Like_I_Do_(David_Guetta,_Martin_Garrix_and_Brooks_song)" title="Like I Do (David Guetta, Martin Garrix and Brooks song)">Like I Do</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> Two days later, he headlined the <a href="/wiki/2018_Winter_Olympics_closing_ceremony" title="2018 Winter Olympics closing ceremony">closing ceremony</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Pyeongchang_County" title="Pyeongchang County">Pyeongchang</a> <a href="/wiki/2018_Winter_Olympics" title="2018 Winter Olympics">2018 Winter Olympic Games</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Pyeongchang_Olympic_Stadium" title="Pyeongchang Olympic Stadium">Pyeongchang Olympic Stadium</a> in <a href="/wiki/South_Korea" title="South Korea">South Korea</a>. He was the closing act of the night, performing his newly released single as well as many others. His setlist is as follows: "Forever", "Together", "Animals", "Like I Do", and "Pizza".<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 20 April 2018, Garrix released his collaboration with Loopers titled "<a href="/wiki/Game_Over_(Martin_Garrix_and_Loopers_song)" title="Game Over (Martin Garrix and Loopers song)">Game Over</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup>  On 15 June, he released the single "<a href="/wiki/Ocean_(Martin_Garrix_song)" title="Ocean (Martin Garrix song)">Ocean</a>", a collaboration with American R&amp;B singer <a href="/wiki/Khalid_(singer)" title="Khalid (singer)">Khalid</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> On 29 July, he headlined the <a href="/wiki/Tomorrowland_(festival)" title="Tomorrowland (festival)">Tomorrowland Belgium</a> 2018 music festival and released the single "<a href="/wiki/High_on_Life_(Martin_Garrix_song)" class="mw-redirect" title="High on Life (Martin Garrix song)">High on Life</a>", a collaboration with singer Bonn, immediately after his closing set ended.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> On 30 July, the music video for "High on Life" was released which contained footage from his Tomorrowland set.
</p><p>Garrix was announced as a resident DJ at Ushuaia Ibiza Beach Hotel, performing on Thursdays from 5 July to 30 August 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> It was announced that he will be bringing guests to perform with him at the said venue. He was also scheduled to be the resident DJ at Hakkasan Nightclub, Omnia Nightclub, and Wet Republic Dayclub starting 2 August.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 10 August 2018, under his 'GRX' alias, he released the single "X's", a collaboration with Dutch DJ <a href="/wiki/CMC$" title="CMC$">CMC$</a> featuring Icona Pop. On 14 September, he released his collaboration with <a href="/wiki/Justin_Mylo" title="Justin Mylo">Justin Mylo</a> featuring <a href="/wiki/Dewain_Whitmore_Jr." title="Dewain Whitmore Jr.">Dewain Whitmore Jr.</a> titled "<a href="/wiki/Burn_Out_(Martin_Garrix_and_Justin_Mylo_song)" title="Burn Out (Martin Garrix and Justin Mylo song)">Burn Out</a>". The music video was released on the same day.
</p><p>It was announced on social media that Garrix was releasing five songs in five days, in a similar manner to the single releases of his <i>Seven</i> EP in 2016. The songs are all part of the <i><a href="/wiki/Bylaw_(EP)" title="Bylaw (EP)">Bylaw</a></i> EP, and are: "<a href="/wiki/Breach_(Walk_Alone)" title="Breach (Walk Alone)">Breach (Walk Alone)</a>" with Blinders, "<a href="/wiki/Yottabyte_(song)" title="Yottabyte (song)">Yottabyte</a>", "Latency" with <a href="/wiki/Dyro" title="Dyro">Dyro</a>, "<a href="/wiki/Access_(song)" title="Access (song)">Access</a>", and "<a href="/wiki/Waiting_for_Tomorrow_(Martin_Garrix_and_Pierce_Fulton_song)" title="Waiting for Tomorrow (Martin Garrix and Pierce Fulton song)">Waiting for Tomorrow</a>" with <a href="/wiki/Pierce_Fulton" title="Pierce Fulton">Pierce Fulton</a> featuring <a href="/wiki/Mike_Shinoda" title="Mike Shinoda">Mike Shinoda</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> In the same month, Garrix performed at the <a href="/wiki/2018_Singapore_Grand_Prix" title="2018 Singapore Grand Prix">F1 Singapore Grand Prix</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In October 2018, Garrix was ranked number one on <a href="/wiki/DJ_Mag" title="DJ Mag">DJ Mag</a>'s annual Top 100 DJs list, winning for the third time in a row. His first win in 2016 made him the youngest DJ to top the poll. The awarding ceremony was held onstage at the Amsterdam ArenA during the 2018 Amsterdam Dance Event (ADE) where Garrix headlined.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 1 November 2018, he released the single "<a href="/wiki/Dreamer_(Martin_Garrix_song)" title="Dreamer (Martin Garrix song)">Dreamer</a>" featuring American singer <a href="/wiki/Mike_Yung" title="Mike Yung">Mike Yung</a>. He released his next single "Glitch", with long-time collaborator <a href="/wiki/Julian_Jordan" title="Julian Jordan">Julian Jordan</a> on 14 December.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="2019:_Headlining_festivals_.26_song_leaks"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2019:_Headlining_festivals_&amp;_song_leaks">2019: Headlining festivals &amp; song leaks</span></h3>
<p>Garrix announced an upcoming collaboration with Bonn, titled "No Sleep".<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> The single was released in February 2019, along with the music video.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In February 2019, he performed at the <a href="/wiki/Ultra_Music_Festival" title="Ultra Music Festival">Ultra Music Festival</a> Australia, a two-day festival held in Sydney and Melbourne.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup>
In March 2019, he headlined <a href="/wiki/Tomorrowland" title="Tomorrowland">Tomorrowland</a> Winter, held in France, and Ultra Music Festival, held in Miami.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In October 2019, Garrix lost his place as <a href="/wiki/DJ_Mag#Top_100_DJs" title="DJ Mag">number 1 DJ</a> to Belgian DJs <a href="/wiki/Dimitri_Vegas_%26_Like_Mike" title="Dimitri Vegas &amp; Like Mike">Dimitri Vegas &amp; Like Mike</a>, whom he beat to number 1 in 2016, after spending a consecutive three years at the top. Garrix finished the 2019 polls in second place.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> The next month, he announced on his Instagram account he have ended up his relationship for over three years with Dutch model Charelle Schriek.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 24 December 2019, Spinnin' Records won the appeal from the court ruling of the Higher Court of Leeuwarden, suggesting that Garrix did not have the right to break his agreement prematurely with Spinnin' and MusicAllstars Management.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A few days after Spinnin' Records won the appeal, Martin's computer was hacked by an unknown assailant where the hacker stole and leaked a handful of unreleased music including "Rewind Repeat It".<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="quotebox pullquote floatright" style="width:33%;&#32;;"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r887775652">.mw-parser-output .quotebox{background-color:#F9F9F9;border:1px solid #aaa;box-sizing:border-box;padding:10px;font-size:88%;max-width:100%}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatleft{margin:0.5em 1.4em 0.8em 0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatright{margin:0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.centered{margin:0.5em auto 0.8em auto}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatleft p,.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatright p{font-style:inherit}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-title{background-color:#F9F9F9;text-align:center;font-size:larger;font-weight:bold}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote.quoted:before{font-family:"Times New Roman",serif;font-weight:bold;font-size:large;color:gray;content:" “ ";vertical-align:-45%;line-height:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote.quoted:after{font-family:"Times New Roman",serif;font-weight:bold;font-size:large;color:gray;content:" ” ";line-height:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .left-aligned{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .right-aligned{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .center-aligned{text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .quotebox cite{display:block;font-style:normal}@media screen and (max-width:360px){.mw-parser-output .quotebox{min-width:100%;margin:0 0 0.8em!important;float:none!important}}</style>
<div class="quotebox-quote left-aligned" style="">I am delighted with the ruling of the Higher Court that we made valid agreements with Martijn at the time, which should have been respected. This statement confirms that the accusation of deception or fraud was unjustified. Even though I have since sold Spinnin' Records and MusicAllStars Management, those accusations were also aimed at me personally. I look back with pride on a successful collaboration with Martijn and wish him the best in his further career.</div>
<p><cite class="left-aligned" style="">—Eelko van Kooten<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup></cite>
</p>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2020:_New_collaborations">2020: New collaborations</span></h3>
<p>In February 2020, Garrix released a track called "<a href="/wiki/Drown_(Martin_Garrix_song)" title="Drown (Martin Garrix song)">Drown</a>" with singer Clinton Kane.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> For the 2020 <a href="/wiki/Koningsdag" title="Koningsdag">King's Day</a> celebrations in April, Garrix played a set from the rooftop of A'Dam tower in <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam" title="Amsterdam">Amsterdam</a> in place of the usual festival's cancellation due to the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic" title="COVID-19 pandemic">COVID-19 pandemic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> The next month, he released the single "<a href="/wiki/Higher_Ground_(Martin_Garrix_song)" title="Higher Ground (Martin Garrix song)">Higher Ground</a>", featuring singer <a href="/wiki/John_Martin_(singer)" title="John Martin (singer)">John Martin</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Brand_endorsement_and_modelling">Brand endorsement and modelling</span></h2>
<p>In 2015, Garrix was an ambassador for Swiss brand <a href="/wiki/TAG_Heuer" title="TAG Heuer">TAG Heuer</a>. The announcement was made in October 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2017, Garrix was an ambassador for Italian brand <a href="/wiki/Armani_Exchange" class="mw-redirect" title="Armani Exchange">Armani Exchange</a>’s "Fall Winter 2017" campaign. The announcement was made in July 2017, along with the release of the promotional photographs on social media.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> The promotional video, featuring Garrix wearing the brand's clothing and eyewear line, was released in August 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2018, Garrix was once again an ambassador for Armani Exchange. The promotional video for the brand's "Fall Winter 2018" campaign was released in August 2018, featuring Garrix wearing the brand's new clothing line. His collaboration track with Loopers, "Game Over", was used for the video.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> The behind-the-scenes footage during the filming was also released by Armani Exchange.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Garrix became an ambassador for <a href="/wiki/Axe_(brand)" title="Axe (brand)">AXE</a>, launched a limited-edition Martin Garrix body spray, which was launching on September 14, 2018. To promote the partnership and the product launch, AXE and Garrix released his music video for "Burn Out" in collaboration with the brand and created by AXE's global creative agency <a href="/wiki/72andSunny" title="72andSunny">72andSunny</a> Amsterdam.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Philanthropy">Philanthropy</span></h2>
<p>In May 2016, Garrix headlined an event in Los Angeles<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> with all proceeds going to the non-profit organization Fuck Cancer, dedicated to early detection, prevention and providing support to those affected by cancer.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In November 2016, Garrix started his India tour with a special charity show in Mumbai with over 62,000 in attendance.<sup id="cite_ref-TheBanginBeats1_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TheBanginBeats1-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> Hosted at the Mahalaxmi Racecourse, the charity event's purpose was to educate Indian children with the proceeds from the show being donated to Magic Bus, who will be supporting the education of 10,000 children across the country.<sup id="cite_ref-TheBanginBeats1_120-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TheBanginBeats1-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 24 February 2017, Garrix was announced as an "international friend" for <a href="/wiki/SOS_Children%27s_Villages" title="SOS Children&#39;s Villages">SOS Children's Village</a> in <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a>, a non-profit organization that "builds families for orphaned, abandoned, and other vulnerable children around the world".<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> Speaking to <i><a href="/wiki/Billboard_(magazine)" title="Billboard (magazine)">Billboard</a></i>, he said "it is awful that so many children around the world don't have the support of a caring family". Following the <a href="/wiki/2017_Puebla_earthquake" title="2017 Puebla earthquake">Mexico earthquake</a> in 2017, Garrix donated $10000 of his fee as <a href="/wiki/Ultra_Music_Festival" title="Ultra Music Festival">Ultra Mexico</a> line up.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 28 February 2019, Garrix visited the <a href="/wiki/SOS_Children%27s_Villages" title="SOS Children&#39;s Villages">SOS Children's Village</a> in <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a> while on tour for <a href="/wiki/Ultra_South_Africa" title="Ultra South Africa">Ultra South Africa</a>. During his visit Garrix performed a one-hour DJ set to an excited crowd of one hundred children and young people, some aged just three years old and accompanied by their SOS mothers.
</p><p>In September 2019, Garrix held a show in his home country <a href="/wiki/Holland" title="Holland">Holland</a> with all proceeds going towards the Warchild Holland Charity. During this show, he raised more than €270,000.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> In June 2020, he was appeared in a public service announcement alongside other celebs for War Child, an organization that supports and empowers the most vulnerable communities, focusing on children and their families.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Book">Book</span></h2>
<p>On 23 August 2018, Garrix posted a picture of the cover of his then upcoming book <i>Martin Garrix Life = Crazy</i>, containing photographs of his career life and personal life. The photographs featured in the book were taken by Louis Van Baar. The book was released in October 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
